# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

68-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the HTTP filter chain extension mechanism in Envoy. Here's what I found:

## Summary

The HTTP filter chain extension architecture in Envoy is built on three core components:

### **1. Core Infrastructure Files:**
- **envoy/http/filter_factory.h** - Defines `FilterChainManager`, `FilterFactoryCb`, and `FilterChainFactory` interfaces
- **envoy/http/filter.h** - Defines `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks`, `StreamFilter`, `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`
- **envoy/server/filter_config.h** - Defines the filter configuration factory hierarchy with `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` and `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory`

### **2. Implementation Files:**
- **source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc** - Per-request filter chain execution engine with `FilterManager` and `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl`
- **source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h/cc** - Filter chain utility for converting factory callbacks to active filters
- **source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h/cc** - Dynamic filter configuration support via ECDS
- **source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h** - Common template base for filter implementations

### **Key Design:**
- **Factory Pattern**: Filters are created at configuration time as closures (`FilterFactoryCb`), instantiated at stream time
- **Registry**: Filters register via `REGISTER_FACTORY()` macro for dynamic discovery
- **Chain Execution**: `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` executes the filter factory callback, which uses `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` to add filters to the stream

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, all relevant symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the architecture and execution flow.

The connection manager bases further\\n36:  * filter invocations on the return code of the previous filter.\\n37:  */\\n38: enum class FilterHeadersStatus {\\n39:   // Continue filter chain iteration.\\n40:   Continue,\\n41:   // Do not iterate for headers on any of the remaining filters in the chain.\\n42:   //\\n43:   // Returning FilterDataStatus::Continue from decodeData()/encodeData() or calling\\n44:   // continueDecoding()/continueEncoding() MUST be called if continued filter iteration is desired.\\n45:   //\\n46:   // Note that if a local reply was sent, no further iteration for headers as well as data and\\n47:   // trailers for the current filter and the filters following will happen. A local reply can be\\n48:   // triggered via sendLocalReply() or encodeHeaders().\\n49:   StopIteration,\\n50:   // Continue headers iteration to remaining filters, but delay ending the stream. This status MUST\\n51:   // NOT be returned when end_stream is already set to false.\\n52:   //\\n53:   // Used when a filter wants to add a body to a headers-only request/response, but this body is not\\n54:   // readily available. Delaying end_stream allows the filter to add the body once it's available\\n55:   // without stopping headers iteration.\\n56:   //\\n57:   // The filter is responsible to continue the stream by providing a body through calling\\n58:   // injectDecodedDataToFilterChain()/injectEncodedDataToFilterChain(), possibly multiple times\\n59:   // if the body needs to be divided into several chunks. The filter may need to handle\\n60:   // watermark events when injecting a body, see:\\n61:   // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/source/docs/flow_control.md.\\n62:   //\\n63:   // The last call to inject data MUST have end_stream set to true to conclude the stream.\\n64:   // If the filter cannot provide a body the stream should be reset.\\n65:   //\\n66:   // Adding a body through calling addDecodedData()/addEncodedData() then\\n67:   // continueDecoding()/continueEncoding() is currently NOT supported and causes an assert failure.\\n68:   //\\n69:   // Adding trailers in this scenario is currently NOT supported.\\n70:   //\\n71:   // The filter MUST NOT attempt to continue the stream without providing a body using\\n72:   // continueDecoding()/continueEncoding().\\n73:   //\\n74:   // TODO(yosrym93): Support adding a body in this case by calling addDecodedData()/addEncodedData()\\n75:   // then continueDecoding()/continueEncoding(). To support this a new FilterManager::IterationState\\n76:   // needs to be added and set when a filter returns this status in\\n77:   // FilterManager::decodeHeaders/FilterManager::encodeHeaders()\\n78:   // Currently, when a filter returns this, the IterationState is Continue. discovery of HTTP filters\\n2. **Filter Context**: Provides metadata about filter configuration during chain creation\\n3. **Per-Request Filter Chain Execution**: Manages runtime instantiation and execution of filters for each HTTP stream\\n\\n## Core Files\\n\\n### Filter Factory Interfaces (envoy/http/filter_factory.h)\\nDefines the core abstractions for HTTP filter chain management:\\n- `FilterFactoryCb`: Type alias for a function that accepts `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` and creates filter instances\\n- `FilterContext`: Struct containing filter configuration name and extension qualified name\\n- `FilterChainManager`: Interface allowing filter factories to apply filter factory callbacks to a manager\\n- `FilterChainFactory`: Interface for creating HTTP filter chains when new streams are created\\n\\n### Filter Interfaces (envoy/http/filter.h)\\nDefines filter types and callbacks:\\n- `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks`: Interface that filter factories use to add filters to the chain\\n- `StreamFilter`: Base interface for HTTP filters\\n- `StreamDecoderFilter`: Interface for decoding path filters\\n- `StreamEncoderFilter`: Interface for encoding path filters\\n\\n### Filter Configuration Registry (envoy/server/filter_config.h)\\nDefines factory interfaces for filter registration:\\n- `HttpFilterConfigFactoryBase`: Base factory class with protocol options support\\n- `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory`: Factory interface for downstream HTTP filters; registered in the registry\\n- `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory`: Factory interface for upstream HTTP filters to clusters\\n- These factories implement `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` to convert protobuf config into `FilterFactoryCb` functions\\n\\n## Implementation Files\\n\\n### Filter Manager (source/common/http/filter_manager.h and .cc)\\nThe per-request filter chain execution engine:\\n- `FilterManager`: Main implementation managing active filters in a stream\\n- `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl`: Nested class implementing `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` interface\\n- Manages decoder/encoder filter lists and iteration state\\n- Implements `applyFilterFactoryCb()` to execute filter factory callbacks\\n- Invokes filters in the correct order (decoder path, then encoder path)\\n\\n### Filter Chain Helper (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h and .cc)\\nStateful filter chain factory support:\\n- `FilterChainUtility`: Static utility for creating HTTP filter chains from factory lists\\n  - `createFilterChainForFactories()`: Converts filter factory callbacks into active filter instances\\n  - `FilterFactoryProvider`: Wraps a filter config provider and disabled status\\n  - `FilterFactoriesList`: List of filter factory providers\\n- `FilterChainHelper`: Template class for processing filter configurations\\n  - `processFilters()`: Converts protobuf filter configs into filter factory callbacks\\n  - Handles both static and dynamic (ECDS) filter configurations\\n  - Validates filter dependencies and terminal filter constraints\\n- Creates singleton `DownstreamFilterConfigProviderManager` and `UpstreamFilterConfigProviderManager`\\n\\n### Dynamic Filter Configuration (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h and .cc)\\nSupport for dynamic filter discovery via ECDS:\\n- `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl`: Template class implementing dynamic filter config provider\\n  - `instantiateFilterFactory()`: Converts protobuf messages to `NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb`\\n  - Supports both `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` and `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory`\\n- Manages filter configuration subscription and warm-up\\n- Handles filter factory resolution from registry by type URL\\n\\n### Common Factory Base (source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h)\\nTemplate base class for filter factory implementations:\\n- `CommonFactoryBase`: Generic template implementing both `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` and `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory`\\n- Provides `createFilterFactoryFromProtoTyped()` for type-safe factory creation\\n- Reduces boilerplate for individual filter implementations\\n\\n## Extension Points\\n\\nEach HTTP filter implements a factory class (e.g., `source/extensions/filters/http/*/config.h`) that:\\n1. Derives from `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` or `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory` (or both)\\n2. Implements `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` to parse configuration and return a `FilterFactoryCb`\\n3. Registers itself via `REGISTER_FACTORY()` macro in the `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` registry\\n4. The returned `FilterFactoryCb` captures configuration state and creates filter instances on invocation\\n\\n## Execution Flow\\n\\n1. Configuration Phase:\\n   - Filter configurations are loaded via protobuf\\n   - `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` looks up factories in registry\\n   - Each factory's `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` creates a `FilterFactoryCb` closure\\n   - Closures are stored in a `FilterFactoriesList`\\n\\n2. Stream Creation Phase:\\n   - `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` is invoked per new HTTP stream\\n   - Calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the factory list\\n   - This function iterates through factories and calls `manager.applyFilterFactoryCb()`\\n\\n3. Filter Instantiation Phase:\\n   - `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` invokes each `FilterFactoryCb` with a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl`\\n   - The closure executes its captured configuration and calls callbacks to add filters\\n   - Filters are added to appropriate lists (decoder filters, encoder filters)\\n\\n4. Stream Processing Phase:\\n   - `FilterManager` iterates through filters on headers, data, trailers\\n   - Respects filter return codes to control chain progression\\n   - Handles filter callbacks for headers/data injection and local replies\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories defer actual filter creation until stream time, enabling:\\n  - Configuration validation at startup\\n  - Lazy filter instantiation only for active streams\\n  - Filter instance per-stream isolation\\n\\n- **Callback-based Composition**: `FilterFactoryCb` closures capture configuration and create filters dynamically\\n\\n- **Registry Pattern**: `REGISTER_FACTORY()` enables dynamic filter discovery without compile-time dependencies\\n\\n- **Template Specialization**: `FilterChainHelper` and `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` use templates to handle both downstream and upstream contexts\\n\\n- **Visitor Pattern**: `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` allows filters to be added without filter manager knowing specific filter types\"\n}\n",
